    Jaundice from Alcohol: Mash the white bark of the Xianping tree root and soak it in rice vinegar overnight. In the early morning, on an empty stomach, take one to two sheng of it warm.

    Food-Related Yellow Swelling with Gas and Chest Fullness: Use non-boring soap pods, peel them, and mix the charred and vinegar-treated powder (one qian) with seven seeds of the Ba Dou after removing the oily film. Grind it with diluted vinegar to make a paste, form into pills the size of a hemp seed, and take three pills after meals with aged tangerine peel soup, three times a day. Increase by one pill every other day until recovery.

    Seasonal Yellowing: Cut five sheng of bamboo leaves, seven sheng of wheat, and three liang of gypsum. Boil with a maximum of one and a half dou of water until obtaining seven sheng, and take the entire dose finely.

    Fatigue Yellow Jaundice: When the body feels heavy with insomnia, eyes red like vermilion, and a mass below the heart like a lump, the condition is critical. It’s beneficial to cauterize under the tongue, moxibustion on the Xinshu and Guanyuan points—two to seven times; use the ashes of a woman’s undergarment, take two qian with wine.

    Damp-Heat Yellow Jaundice: Grind the burned essence of crab into powder, form pills the size of Chinese parasol seeds with wine, and take fifty pills each time, twice daily with warm water.

    Jaundice from Alcohol and Other Types of Jaundice: Raise field snails in water for several days, remove the mud, crush them raw, mix with good wine, filter through cloth, and drink the juice three times a day for effectiveness.

    Yellow Jaundice from Alcohol: Raise small snails to remove soil, cook and eat daily, and drink the juice for effectiveness.[93p]

    After vomiting blood, if one's body and face turn yellow and the blood is like a basin, and no medications are effective: take ten snails, wash away the mud, crush them, let them sit overnight, and take the clear liquid by dawn, drinking it two or three times will stop the bleeding and lead to recovery. A person tried this remedy with success.

    For seasonal jaundice: take a golden-footed yellow hen, treat it as food, boil it, and eat it, also drink the broth until it's finished, and repeat if necessary. A little salt and fermented soybeans can also be added.

    For severe jaundice: use half a pound of large male chicken, cut it open on its back without plucking the feathers, and attach it to the patient’s chest while it is still warm. Replace it when it cools, changing several chickens daily, and this will draw out the accumulated toxins and lead to recovery. This chicken is toxic and should not be eaten, nor will dogs eat it.

    For facial jaundice: use two parts of chicken dung, small beans, and sorghum flour, grind them into powder, divide into three doses, and take with water. There should be a yellow sweat released.

    For an emergency treatment for jaundice: use one egg, burn the shell to ashes, grind it, mix with one measure of vinegar, and take it warm. If there are worms in the nose, it will be effective. If the body is extremely yellow, take only three eggs for miraculous results.

    For seasonal jaundice: soak the egg in vinegar overnight and swallow the white parts a few at a time.

    • For alcohol-induced jaundice with a pale face and abdominal bloating that does not subside: Take one pig kidney, cut it open with seven incisions, mix in ten grams of kudzu root powder, blend well, and roast each side three and a half times.     　　黄疸，遍身如金色：瓜蒂一十四个，母丁香一个，黍米四十九粒，先捣瓜蒂为末，次入二味，同为细末，每用半字，夜卧，令病人先噙水一口，两鼻内各半字，吐了水，令病人便睡，至夜或明日，取下黄水，旋用熟帛搵了，直候水定，便服黄连散。病轻者五日，重者半月。

    Jaundice: The skin turns golden yellow; use fourteen gourd stems, one mother clove, and forty-nine grains of millet. First, grind the gourd stems into a fine powder, then mix in the other two ingredients to make a fine powder. Use half a dose at night.     Yellow Jaundice: Take a small amount of bear gall, mix with water and take orally.

    Acupuncture

    The "Jia Yi Jing" states: For jaundice, needle the spine.
    For jaundice with a tendency to yawn, fullness under the ribs, the spleen point governs it.
    For jaundice with yellow eyes, the Laogong point governs it.
    For those excessively sleepy, with limbs unwilling to move and yellowing of the body, moxibustion is applied at the point five cun below the elbow on both arms alternately. For jaundice with heat and a propensity for thirst, the Taichong point governs it.[98p]

    　　身黄，时有微热，不嗜食，膝内内踝前痛，少气，身体重，中封主之。　　消渴黄疸，足一寒一热，舌纵烦满，然谷主之。　　《千金方》曰：章门，主伤饱身黄。　　中封、五里，主身黄，时有微热。
    　　脊中，主黄疸，腹满，不能食。
    　　脾俞、胃管，主黄疸。
    　　疸病，正面所取诸穴：寅门、上龂里、上腭、侠人中、侠承浆、舌下、唇里、颞颥、巨阙、上脘、阴缝。　　寅门穴：从鼻头直入发际，度取通绳，分为三断，绳取一分，入发际，当绳头针，是穴治马黄、黄疸等病。　　上龂里穴：正当人中及唇。针三锃，治马黄、黄疸等病。　　上腭穴：入口里边，在上缝赤白脉是。针三锃，治马黄、黄疸、四时等病。　　舌下穴：侠舌两边针，治黄疸等病。　　唇里穴：正当承浆里边，逼齿龂。针三锃，治马黄、黄疸、寒暑温疫等病。　　颞颥穴：在眉眼尾中间，上下有来去络脉，是。针灸之，治四时寒暑所苦，疸气温病等。[99p]

    The body appears yellow, with occasional mild heat, loss of appetite, pain in the inner knees and ankles, shortness of breath, and a heavy body; this leads to a diagnosis of jaundice. Thirst and yellowing of the skin are accompanied by one cold foot and one hot foot, a tongue that is wide and full, which indicates another cause. According to the "Thousand Gold Prescription": the Zhangmen point is used for injuries from excessive eating causing jaundice. The Zhongfeng and Wuli points are associated with jaundice, often with mild heat present.

    The spine corresponds to jaundice, fullness in the abdomen, and inability to eat.

    The Pishu and Weiguan points are also related to jaundice.

    For jaundice diseases, the following points should be used: Yimen, Shangyinli, Shangyan, Xiaorenzhong, Xiechengjiang, under the tongue, inside the lips, Tianjiao, Juque, Shangguan, and Yinfeng.

    Yimen point: It is located directly from the tip of the nose to the hairline; measure out a length and divide it into thirds, with one third marking the entry at the hairline where the needle is inserted; this point treats equine jaundice and other related diseases.

    Shangyinli point: Located at the philtrum and lips. Needling three times treats equine jaundice and other similar diseases.

    Shangyan point: Inside the mouth along the upper seam of red and white veins. Needling three times treats equine jaundice, jaundice, and seasonal illnesses.

    Under the tongue point: Needling both sides of the tongue treats jaundice.

    Inside the lips point: Aligned with the Chengjiang point, positioned closely to the teeth. Needling three times treats equine jaundice, jaundice, and diseases from cold and hot climates, as well as epidemics.

    Tianjiao point: Located in the middle of the eyebrow and the tail of the eye, with ascending and descending connective veins. Moxibustion is used here to treat the suffering from seasonal cold and heat, along with jaundice and febrile diseases.[99p]

    　　侠人中穴：火针，治马黄黄疸疫通身并黄，语音已不转者。　　侠承浆穴：去承浆两边各一寸。治马黄、急疫等病。　　巨阙穴：在心下一寸。灸七壮，治马黄、黄疸、急疫等病。　　上脘穴：在心下二寸。灸七壮，治马黄、黄疸等病。　　男阴缝穴：拔阴反向上。灸治马黄、黄疸等病。若女人，玉门是穴。男女针灸无在。　　治疸病，覆面所取诸穴：风府、热府、肺腧、心腧、肝腧、脾腧、肾腧、脚后根。　　风府穴：在项后入发际一寸，去上骨一寸。针之，治头中百病，马黄、黄疸等病。　　热府穴：在第二节下，两旁相去各一寸五分。针灸无在。治马黄、黄疸等病。[100p]

    Translation:

    "Xia Ren Zhongxue (Cavern Point): Huo Zhen (Fire Needle), treats horse jaundice and epidemic diseases characterized by widespread yellowing, where the voice has not yet changed.

    Xia Chengjiang Point: Located one inch on each side of Chengjiang. Treats horse jaundice, acute epidemic diseases, and similar ailments.

    Juque Point: Situated one inch beneath the heart. Moxibustion of seven strong applications treats horse jaundice, yellowing, acute epidemics, and other illnesses.

    Shangguan Point: Located two inches beneath the heart. Moxibustion of seven strong applications treats horse jaundice, yellowing, and similar ailments.

    Nan Yin Feng Point: Pull the male organ upwards. Moxibustion treats horse jaundice, yellowing, etc. For women, Yumen is the point. There is no distinction in acupuncture and moxibustion between men and women.

    For treating jaundice, the following points are used: Fengfu, Refu, Feishu, Xinshu, Gan Shu, Pishu, Shen Shu, and the root of the foot.

    Fengfu Point: Located one inch into the hairline at the back of the neck, one inch above the upper bone. Acupuncture here treats various diseases in the head, including horse jaundice and yellowing.

    Refu Point: Located below the second joint, with one and a half inches on each side. There is no distinction in acupuncture and moxibustion. Treats horse jaundice, yellowing, and similar conditions."[100p]

    　　肺腧穴，从大椎数第三椎，两旁相去各一寸五分。灸主黄疸，通治百毒病。　　心腧穴：从肺腧数第二椎，两旁相去各一寸五分。　　肝腧穴：从心腧数第四椎，两旁相去各一寸五分。　　脾腧穴：从肝腧数第二椎，两旁相去各一寸五分。　　肾腧穴：从脾腧数第三椎，两旁相去。各一寸五分。　　脚后跟穴：在白肉后际。针灸随便。治马黄、黄疸、寒暑诸毒等病。　　治疸病，侧面所取诸穴：耳中、颊里、手太阳、臂石子头、钱孔、太冲。　　耳中穴：在耳门孔上横梁是。针灸之，治马黄、黄疸、寒暑疫毒等病。　　颊里穴：从口吻边入，往对颊里，去口一寸。[101p]

    The Lung Shu point is found three vertebrae below the Dazhui point, one and a half inches to each side. It is treated with moxibustion for jaundice and various toxic diseases. The Heart Shu point is located two vertebrae below the Lung Shu point, one and a half inches to each side. The Liver Shu point is four vertebrae below the Heart Shu point, one and a half inches to each side. The Spleen Shu point is two vertebrae below the Liver Shu point, one and a half inches to each side. The Kidney Shu point is three vertebrae below the Spleen Shu point, one and a half inches to each side. The Heel point is located at the back of the heel. Acupuncture is performed casually. It treats diseases like horse yellow, jaundice, and various toxic conditions. For treating jaundice, the supplementary points on the side include: the ear center, inside the cheek, hand Taiyang, the elbow, the aperture, and the Tai Chong. The Ear center point is located on the horizontal beam above the ear gate. Acupuncture here treats conditions like horse yellow, jaundice, and various toxic diseases. The Inside Cheek point is accessed by entering from the edge of the mouth, directed towards the inside of the cheek, one inch away from the mouth.[101p]

    针，主治马黄、黄疸、寒暑温疫等病。颊两边同法。　　手太阳穴：手小指端。灸随年壮，治黄疸。　　臂石子头穴：还取病人手，自捉臂，从腕中太渊文向上一夫，接白肉际。灸七壮，治马黄、黄疸等病。　　钱孔穴：度乳至脐中，屈肋头骨是。灸百壮，治黄疸。　　太冲穴：针灸随便，治马黄、温疫[温疫　原作「黄温疫毒」，据《千金》卷十伤寒发黄改。]等病。　　《医学纲目》曰：黄疸，腕骨三分，灸七壮；中脘，补。　　黄疸发虚，伤寒饮食过多，取脘骨一分，涌泉三分，灸百劳、三里、中脘、膏肓。　　黄疸久久变为黑疸，身黄额黑，或身面俱黄是也。若身不黄，口面黑，于章门主之。《针灸经》云：神门亦治疸。[102p]

    Acupuncture treats conditions such as jaundice, yellowing of the skin, and illnesses caused by cold and heat. The same methods apply to both sides of the cheeks.

    For the hand’s temples: use the tip of the little finger. Moxibustion is applied according to the patient's strength, treating jaundice.

    For the arm’s key point: have the patient grasp their own arm, starting from the wrist and moving upward to the area connecting to the flesh. Moxibustion is performed seven times to treat cases like jaundice.

    For the qiankong point: measure from the nipple to the navel and find the rib head. Moxibustion is applied a hundred times to treat jaundice.

    For the taichong point: acupuncture and moxibustion as needed treat jaundice and febrile illnesses.

    "The Medical Canon" states: Regarding jaundice, apply moxibustion seven times on the wrist three points. The center of the abdomen should be supplemented.

    When jaundice emerges due to a weak constitution, or from an excess of food during a cold, treat the middle point of the abdominal bone and the yongquan point, applying moxibustion to baolao, sanli, zhongwan, and gaohuang a hundred times.

    Prolonged jaundice may turn into black jaundice, with the body appearing yellow and the forehead black, or both body and face may become yellow. If the body is not yellow but the mouth and face are black, treat the zhangmen point. The "Classic of Acupuncture and Moxibustion" also states: The shenmen point can also treat jaundice.[102p]

    　　　　导引

    　　《保生秘要》曰：黄疸，乃湿气氤氲于内，脉络胶固不通，致有此病。先捻背数次，复行通关法以导其血脉，通其内外；后用两手心按两乳下，揉擦数十遍，其丹田气海处，至沥沥有声方止。　　中湿病，色有黄黑肿，用火烧丹田数圈几遍，次行通关法，其汗自出而湿自消。[103p]

    Guiding Techniques

    "The Secret Essentials for Preserving Life" states: Jaundice is caused by dampness lingering internally, which leads to the obstruction of the meridians. To treat this condition, first knead the back several times, then perform the opening techniques to guide the blood flow and ensure connection between the internal and external. Afterwards, using the palms, press beneath the breasts and rub several dozen times until a sound resembling dripping is heard from the lower abdomen.

    In cases of damp-related illness, the color may appear yellowish-black and swollen. Utilize heat to apply to the lower abdomen several times, followed by the opening techniques, allowing sweat to emerge and dampness to dissipate.[103p]

    　　　　医案

    　　《儒门事亲》曰：蔡寨成家一童子，年十五岁，病疸一年，面黄如金，遍身浮肿乏力，惟食盐与焦物。戴人以茶调散吐之，涌涎一盂；临晚又以舟车丸七八十粒，通经散三钱，下四五行。待六七日，又以舟车丸、浚川散下四五行，盐与焦物见而恶之，面色变红。后再以茶调散涌之，出痰二升，方能愈矣。
    　　又有一男子作赘，偶病疸，善食而瘦，四肢不举，面黄无力，其妇翁欲弃之，其女子不肯，曰：我已生二子矣，更适他乎？妇翁本农者，招婿意欲作劳，见其病甚，每日辱诟。人教之饵胆矾丸、三棱丸，了不关涉，针灸祈禳，百无一济。戴人见之，不诊而疗，使服涌剂，去积痰宿水一斗，又以泄水丸、通经散，下四五十行不止。戴人命以冰水一盂饮之，立止。次服平胃散等，间服槟榔丸，五七日黄退力生。盖脾疸之证，湿热与宿谷相搏故也，俗谓之食劳黄。[104p]

    Medical Case

    The "Confucian Family Care" states: In Caizhai, there was a boy of fifteen years old, suffering from jaundice for a year. His face was as yellow as gold, his body swollen and weak, and he could only eat salt and burnt food. A practitioner used tea to mix a powder, which made him vomit a bowl of phlegm. Later, in the evening, he took seven to eight pills of a certain medicine and three qian of another mixture, which he expelled in four to five actions. After waiting six to seven days, he took more pills and another mixture, expelling four to five actions again. He began to detest salt and burnt food, and his complexion turned red. Afterwards, he used tea to induce vomiting again, bringing out two sheng of phlegm, which finally led to his recovery.

    Additionally, there was a man who developed a lump while suffering from jaundice. He had a good appetite but was thin, unable to lift his limbs, and his face was yellow and weak. His mother-in-law wanted to abandon him, but his daughter refused, saying: "I have already borne two sons; how can I marry another?" The mother-in-law, who was originally a farmer, wanted her son-in-law to work hard, but seeing his severe illness, she scolded him daily. People suggested he take gallbladder pills and a mixture with three angles, but they were of no help. Acupuncture and spells brought no relief either.

    A practitioner saw him and treated him without diagnosis, administering an expelling agent that removed a斗 (about 10 liters) of stagnant phlegm and water. He then prescribed a laxative pill and another mixture, causing him to expel four to five dozen times. The practitioner ordered him to drink a bowl of ice water, which immediately stopped the expulsion. He next took a remedy for the stomach and intermittently took betel nut pills. After five to seven days, his yellow complexion faded and strength returned. The symptoms of jaundice from the spleen were due to damp heat clashing with accumulated food, commonly referred to as "food labor jaundice."[104p]

    　　朱葛周黄刘三家，各有仆病黄疸。戴人曰：仆役之职，饮食寒热，风暑湿寒，寻常触冒也，恐难调摄，虚费治功。其二家留仆于戴人所，从其饮饵。其一仆不离主人，执役。三人同服苦参散以涌之，又服三花神佑丸下之，五日之间，果二仆愈而一仆不愈，如其言。
    　　安喜赵君玉为掾省日，病发遍身黄，往问医者。医云：君乃阳明证，公等与麻知己皆受训于张戴人，是商议吃大黄者，难与论病。君玉不悦，自揣无别病，乃取三花神佑丸八十粒，服之不动。乃悟曰：予之湿热甚矣，此药尚不动。以舟车丸、浚川散作剂，大下一斗，粪多结者，一夕退黄。君玉由此益信戴人之言。
    　　蔡寨一女病黄，遍身浮肿，面如金色，困乏无力，不思饮饵，惟喜食生物泥煤之属。先以苦剂蒸饼为丸，涌痰一碗；又舟车丸、通经散下五七行如墨汁；更以导饮丸，磨食散气，不数日肌肉如初。[105p]

    Zhu, Ge, Zhou, Huang, and Liu, the three families, each had a servant afflicted with jaundice. Dairen said: "In the role of servants, their diet and exposure to cold and heat, as well as wind, summer, dampness, and cold, often cause such ailments. It is difficult to treat and manage, resulting in wasted efforts." Thus, two families kept their servants at Dairen's place, following his dietary recommendations. One servant did not leave his master and continued to work. The three of them all took Ku Shen powder to induce vomiting and then took Sanhua Shenyuan pills to assist digestion. Within five days, indeed, two servants recovered while one did not, as predicted.

    Mr. Zhao Yuyuan of Anxi became ill with widespread yellowing of the skin and sought a physician's advice. The doctor said: "You have the Yangming disease; you and others have trained under Zhang Dairen, discussing the taking of Dahuang, so it's difficult for us to talk about this illness." Mr. Yuyuan was displeased, believing he had no other illness, and took eighty Sanhua Shenyuan pills but did not improve. He then realized: "My damp heat is severe; this medicine still does not work." Using Zhou Che pills and Jun Chuan powder as remedies, he induced a major purge, resulting in significant bowel movement, and within one evening, his jaundice receded. This experience further reinforced Mr. Yuyuan's trust in Dairen's words.

    A girl from Cai Zhai suffered from jaundice, with extreme swelling, a complexion like gold, fatigue, and a lack of appetite, only inclined to eat raw foods similar to mud and coal. Initially, a bitter agent was made into pills, inducing a bowl of phlegm; followed by Zhou Che pills and Tong Jing powder, inducing several bowel movements like ink; additionally, Daoyin pills and Mo Shi powder were used to relieve gas. Within a few days, her muscles returned to their original state.[105p]

    　　《丹溪心法》曰：一妇人四月内产，发黄，四肢倦怠，食少，经事不来，时发热，脉弦。用白朮一两，人参、秦艽、丹皮、生地、木通、柴胡、芍药各半两，川芎、黄芩、干葛各一钱，甘草三分，十二贴，水煎，食前热服而愈。
    　　《卫生宝鉴》曰：元颜正卿丙寅二月间，因官事劳役，饮食不节，心火乘脾，脾气虚弱，又以恚怒气逆伤肝，心下痞满，四肢困倦，身体麻木，次传身目俱黄，微见青色，颜黑，心神烦乱，怔忡不安，兀兀欲吐，口生恶味，饮食迟化，时下完谷，小便癃闭而赤黑，辰巳间发热，日暮则止，至四月尤盛。其子以危急，求请治之，具说其事。诊其脉浮而缓。《金匮要略》云：寸口脉浮为风，缓为痹。痹非中风，四肢苦烦，脾色必黄，瘀热以行。趺阳脉紧为伤脾，风寒相搏，食谷则眩，谷气不消，胃中苦浊，浊气下流，小便不通，阴被其寒，热流膀胱，身体尽黄，名曰谷疸，宜茯苓栀子茵陈汤主之。[106p]

    The "Danxi Heart Method" states: A woman who gives birth in four months presents with a yellow complexion, fatigue in the limbs, reduced appetite, missed menstruation, occasional fever, and a taut pulse. Use one ounce of Atractylodes, half an ounce each of Ginseng, Gentian, Moutan, Rehmannia, Akebia, Bupleurum, and Peony, one dram each of Chuanxiong, Scutellaria, and Kudzu, and three-fifths of an ounce of Licorice. Prepare twelve doses, boil in water, and take hot before meals for recovery.

    The "Treasured Mirror of Health" mentions: In the second month of the Bingyin year, Yuan Yan Zhengqing, due to labor from official duties and irregular eating, had heart fire troubling the spleen, and with weak spleen qi, anger and resentment injured the liver. He experienced distension in the chest, fatigue in the limbs, body numbness, jaundice appearing in the skin and eyes, slight cyanosis, a dark complexion, disturbed spirit, anxiety, a strong urge to vomit, a foul taste in the mouth, delayed digestion, and occasionally difficult urination that was red and dark. He experienced fever between the hours of Chen and Si, which subsided by evening, but intensified in April. His son, worried for his life, sought treatment and explained the situation. When the pulse was examined, it was floating and weak. The "Shanghan Lun" states that a floating pulse at the wrist indicates wind, while a weak pulse indicates blockage. Blockage is not due to wind stroke; the limbs suffer from restlessness, the spleen appears yellow, and there is heat and stagnation. A tense pulse at the Fuyuan point indicates spleen damage, with wind and cold colliding, leading to dizziness upon eating grains, with grain qi not digesting, bitter and turbid fluids in the stomach, turbid qi descending, difficulty in urination, yin affected by cold, heat flowing to the bladder, and the entire body appearing yellow, which is termed "grain jaundice." It requires Fu Ling, Zhi Zi, and Yin Chen Decoction for treatment.[106p]

    　　至元丙寅六月，时雨霖霪，人多病瘟疫。真定韩君祥因劳役过度，渴饮凉茶，及食冷物，遂病头痛，肢节亦疼，身体沉重，胸满不食，自以为外感伤，用通圣散两服。药后添身体困甚，方命医治之。医以百解散发其汗；越四日，以小柴胡汤二服后，加烦热躁渴。又六日，以三一承气汤下之，躁渴尤甚。又投白虎加人参柴胡饮子之类，病愈增。又易医，用黄连解毒汤、朱砂膏、至宝丹之类。至十七日后，病势转增，传变身目俱黄，肢体沉重，背恶寒，皮肤冷，心下痞硬，按之而痛，眼濇不欲开，目睛不了了，懒言语，自汗，小便利，大便了而不了。命予治之，诊其脉紧细，按之虚空，两寸脉短不及本位，此证得之因时热而多饮冷，加以寒凉药过度，肝木乘心，反来侮土，先困其母，后薄其子。经云：薄所不胜，乘所胜也。时值霖雨，乃寒湿相合，此为阴证发黄明也。予以茵陈附子干姜汤主之。[107p]

    In the sixth month of the year Bingyin during the Yuan dynasty, there was continuous rain, and many people fell ill with epidemics. Han Junxiang from Zhen Ding, due to overexertion, drank cold tea and ate cold foods, leading to a headache, pain in his limbs and joints, a feeling of heaviness in his body, fullness in his chest, and inability to eat. He believed it was an external sickness and took Tongsheng powder twice. After taking the medicine, his body felt even more fatigued, prompting him to seek medical treatment.

    The doctor administered a hundred relief powder to induce sweating; four days later, he took Xiao Chai Hu decoction twice, but his agitation, fever, and thirst worsened. Six days later, he was given San Yi Cheng Qi decoction, exacerbating his agitation and thirst. Other prescriptions like Bai Hu decoction with ginseng and Chai Hu infusion were administered, but his condition only deteriorated.

    He changed doctors, who prescribed Huang Lian Jie Du decoction, Zhu Sha ointment, and Zhi Bao pill among others. By the seventeenth day, the illness progressed, showing yellowing of skin and eyes, heaviness in limbs, chills in the back, cold skin, hardness and pain upon pressing the area under the heart, dry eyes that did not wish to open, a tendency to be mute, spontaneous sweating, small loose stools, and incomplete bowel movements. I was ordered to treat him, and upon examining his pulse, it was tight and thin, and when pressed felt hollow. The pulse at the two-inch point was short and inadequate. This condition arose from the combination of seasonal heat and excessive drinking of cold beverages, compounded by an overuse of cold medicines, causing the liver (wood) to overpower the heart, which in turn weakened the spleen (earth).

    As the classics state: "The one who is weak is overpowered by the one who is strong." It was the season of continuous rain, leading to a combination of cold and dampness, which manifested as a yin condition causing jaundice. I prescribed Yin Chen Fuzi Ganjiang decoction to treat him.[107p]

    《内经》云：寒淫于内，治以甘热，佐以苦辛。湿淫所胜，平以苦热，以淡渗之，以苦燥之。附子、干姜辛甘大热，散其中寒，故以为主。半夏、草豆蔻辛热，白朮、陈皮苦甘温，健脾燥湿，故以为臣。生姜辛温以散之，泽泻甘平以渗之，枳实苦微寒泄其痞满，茵陈苦微寒，其气轻浮，佐以姜附，能去肤腠间寒湿而退其黄，故为佐使也。煎服一两，前证减半，再服悉去。又与理中汤服之，数日气得平复。[108p]

    The "Inner Canon" states: Cold infiltrates within; it is treated with sweet warmth, complemented by bitter and pungent agents. When dampness dominates, it must be balanced with bitter heat, diluted with mildness, and dried with bitterness. Aconite and dried ginger are strongly warm and spicy, dispersing the internal cold, thus they are used as the primary ingredients. Pinellia and cardamom are spicy and warm, while white atractylodes and aged tangerine peel are bitter, sweet, and warm, helping to strengthen the spleen and dry dampness, hence they serve as the secondary ingredients. Fresh ginger is spicy and warm to disperse, while licorice is sweet and neutral to help with infiltration. Bitter orange, being slightly cool and bitter, helps relieve fullness, while Artemisia capillaris is slightly cool and bitter, and its light nature helps; paired with ginger and aconite, it can expel cold dampness from the skin and body, thus serving as an assistant. Take one or two doses; if symptoms reduce by half, continue for complete relief. Additionally, take it with the Regulate the Middle Decoction for several days until the energy stabilizes.[108p]

    或者难曰：发黄皆以为热，今暑隆盛之时，又以热药治之何也？予曰：理所当然，不得不然。成无己云：阴证有二：一者，外伤寒邪，阴经受之，或因食冷物，伤太阴经也。二者，始得阳证，以寒治之，寒凉过度，变阳为阴也。今君祥因时令暑热，冷物伤脾，过服寒凉，阴气大胜，阳气欲绝，又值霖雨寒湿相合，发而为黄也。仲景所谓当于寒湿中求之。李思顺云：解之而寒凉过剂，泻之而逐寇伤君，正以此也。圣贤之制，竟敢越哉！或者曰：洁古之学，有自来矣。[109p]

    Some may find it difficult to understand: Why is it thought that yellow indicates heat, and yet during the peak of summer, one uses heat-clearing medicine to treat it? I say: It is natural and must be this way. Cheng Wujǐ states: There are two types of yin syndromes: One arises from external cold pathogens injuring the yin channels, or from consuming cold food, thus harming the Taiyin channel. The second occurs when one initially contracts a yang syndrome, and then treats it with cold, which, if excessive, transforms yang into yin. Now, you have the condition of Mr. Xiang, caused by the summer heat; the consumption of cold food harms the spleen, and overindulgence in cold leads to a dominance of yin qi, with yang qi on the verge of collapse. Additionally, with the convergence of continual rain and cold humidity, it manifests as yellow. This correlates with what Zhongjing said about seeking it amid cold and damp. Li Sishun comments: To resolve it with excessive cold and coolness, or to purge it and chase out the intruder harms the host—this is precisely the case. The sages' principles should not be carelessly neglected! Some might say: The study of cleanliness has been around since ancient times.[109p]

    　　《医学纲目》曰：一妇人年六十岁，病振寒战栗，足太阳寒水也；呵欠喷嚏，足少阳胆也；口中乏津液，足阳明不足也；心中急痛而痞，手少阴受寒，足少阴血滞也；身热又欲近火，热在皮肤，寒在骨髓也；脐下恶寒，丹田有寒也；浑身黄及睛黄，皆寒湿也。余证验之，知其为寒。溺黄赤而黑又频数者，寒湿胜也。病来身重如山，便着床枕者，阴湿盛也。其脉右手关尺命门弦细，按之洪而弦。弦急为寒；加之细者，北方寒水；杂以缓甚者，湿盛出黄色。脉洪大者，心火受制也。左手又按之至骨，举手来实者，壬癸肾旺也。六脉按之俱空虚者，下焦无阳也。用药法，先宜以轻剂去其寒湿，兼退其洪大之脉，以理中加茯苓汤投之，水煎熟，以冰冷与之。此热因寒用，以假寒对足太阳之假热，以干姜辛热泻膀胱之真气，故曰真对真，假对假。若不愈，当以朮附汤与之。按此证虽小便黄赤，亦作寒治者，盖以余证及脉别之也。[110p]

    The "Medical Treatise" states: A woman aged sixty suffers from shivering and chills, indicating cold in the foot's solar channels; yawning and sneezing relate to the foot's lesser yang and gallbladder; lack of saliva in her mouth suggests deficiency in the foot's yang brightness; there is acute pain and fullness in the heart, with the hand's lesser yin affected by cold, and stagnation of blood in the foot's lesser yin. She feels hot but desires proximity to fire, showing heat on the skin while cold resides in the bones. There is cold and discomfort below the navel, indicating cold in the lower dantian; her whole body and eyes show yellow, a sign of cold dampness. I have confirmed this and know it to be cold. Frequent yellow, red, and dark urination denotes excessive cold dampness. When the illness causes her body to feel heavy like a mountain, she immediately lies on her bed; this indicates excess of yin dampness. The pulse at the right wrist shows a thin string at the gate of life and heartbeat; pressing reveals it is strong and string-like. A tense string signifies cold; if it is also delicate, it indicates northern cold waters; if mixed with a very slow pulse, this shows excess dampness leading to yellowish conditions. A strong and broad pulse indicates heart fire is constrained. Pressing the left wrist down to the bone and noting fullness in the hand indicates vitality in the kidneys (water). If all six pulses are empty, there is no yang present in the lower source. As for treatment, I first recommend light doses to dispel the cold dampness, while also reducing the strong pulse, using a formula combining licorice with poria cooked in water to serve cool. This addresses heat brought on by cold, using fictitious cold against the foot's solar channels' false heat and applies the spicy warm properties of ginger to disperse the bladder's true qi, thus saying true against true, false against false. If there is no improvement, I would then prescribe a decoction of atractylodes and aconite. Although this condition presents with yellow and red urination, it still calls for cold treatment based on further symptom analysis and pulse examination.[110p]

    　　一人病身体痛，面黄喘满头痛，自能饮食，大小便如常。予诊之，脉大而虚，鼻塞而烦。予曰：非湿热宿谷相搏，此乃头中寒湿，非茵陈五苓，不可行也。仲景云：湿家病身疼痛，发热面黄而喘，头痛鼻塞而烦，其脉大，自能饮食，腹中和无病，病在头中，寒湿攻鼻故塞，纳药鼻中则愈。仲景无药方，此方见《外台》删繁证云治天行热病，盖通贯脏腑寒湿，沉于骨髓之间，或为黄疸，宜瓜蒂散，即此方也。[111p]

    A person is suffering from body pain, their face is pale, they are short of breath, and have a severe headache. They can still eat and have normal bowel movements. Upon examining them, I found their pulse to be large and weak, their nose is blocked, and they appear restless. I said: It is not caused by damp heat clashing with residual food; this is cold dampness in the head. It cannot be treated with Yinchenhao and Wuling, as it is not suitable. Zhongjing states: In cases of dampness causing body pain, with fever, a yellowish face, shortness of breath, headaches, and nasal congestion, the pulse is large, and the person can still eat. There are no issues in the abdomen, indicating that the illness lies in the head; cold dampness attacking the nose causes the blockage. Medicines taken through the nose can alleviate it. Zhongjing does not provide a prescription, but this formula appears in the "Wai Tai," which discusses treating the heat from seasonal epidemics. It likely harmonizes the cold dampness throughout the organs, penetrating deep into the marrow, and might cause jaundice; hence, the Guati powder is appropriate, which is this formula.[111p]

    　　一舟梢病伤寒发黄鼻酸，通身与目如金色。小便赤而数，大便如常。或者欲用茵陈五苓。予曰：非其治也。小便利，大便如常，则知病不在脏。今眼睛鼻额痛，是病在清道中。清道者华盖，肺之经也。若下大黄，则必腹胀为逆。亦用瓜蒂散，先含水，次(口畜)之鼻中，黄水尽乃愈。
    　　赵宗颜因下之太过生黄，脉沉细迟无力，海藏次第用药，至茵陈附子汤，大效。按海藏次第用药者，谓先投韩氏茵陈茯苓汤，次投茵陈陈皮汤，又次投茵陈附子汤。后赵秀才次第仿此。赵秀才因下之早，黄病，脉寸微尺弱，身冷，次第用药至茵陈四逆汤，大效。
    　　一僧伤寒，发汗不彻，有留热，身面皆黄，多热，期年不愈。医作食黄治之，治不对，病不去。问之，食不减。寻与此药，服五日，病减三分之一；十日，减三分之二；二十日，病悉去。方用茵陈、栀子各三分，秦艽、升麻各四钱，末之，每用三钱，水四合，煎及二合，去滓，食后温服，以和为度。[112p]

    A boat arrived with a patient suffering from a cold that had caused a yellowed nose and sore eyes, and their entire body and eyes appeared golden. The urine was red and frequent, while the bowel movements were normal. Some suggested using Yinchen and Wuling, but I said that was not the correct treatment. With normal bowel movements, it indicates the illness is not in the organs. Now, with pain in the eyes and nose, the issue lies within the pathways of the lungs. If Da Huang (rhubarb) is administered, it would certainly cause abdominal distension as a side effect. One could also use Guati San by first dissolving it in water, then placing it in the nose until the yellow fluid is completely cleared.

    Zhao Zongyan, after excessive purging, developed jaundice with a pulse that was deep, thin, slow, and weak. Gradually, different medicines were administered, reaching Yinchen and Fuzi Decoction, which produced great effects. For the gradual approach, it meant first administering Han's Yinchen and Fuling Decoction, then moving on to Yinchen and Chenpi Decoction, and finally to Yinchen and Fuzi Decoction. Later, Scholar Zhao followed this method step by step. Due to early purging, he experienced jaundice, with a weak and shallow pulse and a cold body. He gradually took medication until reaching Yinchen and Sini Decoction, which had great effects.

    A monk with a cold had not fully sweated out the illness and retained heat, causing his entire face and body to turn yellow and suffer from excessive heat, with a year passing without recovery. The doctor treated it as food poisoning, but that was not the correct approach, and the illness did not resolve. When asked about his diet, it had not decreased. Subsequently, this medicine was given. After five days, his condition improved by one third; after ten days, two thirds; and after twenty days, the illness was completely gone. The formula used was three parts of Yinchen and Zhi Zi, and four qian each of Qin Jiao and Sheng Ma, ground into a powder. Each time, three qian were used, boiled with four cups of water to reduce to two cups, strained, and taken warm after meals, in moderation.[112p]

    　　《医学正传》曰：一男年三十余，得谷疸证，求予治，以胃苓汤去桂加茵陈，数十贴黄退。自以为安，不服药。十数日后，至晚，目盲不见物。予曰：此名雀目。盖湿痰盛而肝火有余也。用獖猪肝煮熟，和夜明砂作丸服之，目遂明如故。来谢。予曰：未也。不早服制肝补脾消痰之剂，必转蛊胀。伊不信，半月后，腹渐胀，痞满，复求治。予仍以胃苓汤，倍二朮，加木通、麦门冬，煎汤下褪金丸，一月平安。
    　　《薛己医案》曰：大司徒李蒲汀南吏部少宰，时患黄疸，当用淡渗之剂。公尚无嗣，犹豫不决。余曰：有是病而用是药。以茵陈五苓散加芩、连、山栀二剂而愈。至辛卯得子，公执余手而笑曰：医方犹公案也，设君避毁语残喘，安得享余年而遂付托之望哉？由是礼遇益厚。
    　　应天王治中，遍身发黄，妄言如狂，苦于胸痛，手不可近，此中焦蓄血为患，用桃仁承气汤一剂，下瘀血而愈。
    [113p]

    The "Principles of Medicine" states: A man over thirty suffered from jaundice and sought my treatment. I prescribed Wei Ling Decoction, removed the cinnamon, and added Yin Chen, using several dozen medicated plasters to reduce the yellowing. He thought himself cured and did not take the medication. After ten days, by evening, his vision failed completely. I said: This is called "sparrow's eye." It is due to excessive damp phlegm and excess liver fire. I instructed him to cook pig liver and mix it with Ming Sha into pills to take, and his vision returned to normal. He came to thank me. I said: Not yet. If you do not take the liver-regulating, spleen-nourishing, phlegm-dispelling medicine early, it will certainly turn into bloating. He did not believe me, but after half a month, his abdomen gradually became bloated and full, and he sought treatment again. I prescribed Wei Ling Decoction once more, doubling the herbs, adding Mu Tong and Mai Men Dong, and prepared a decoction to take with the gold-reducing pills. After a month, he was well.

    The "Medical Case of Xue Ji" states: The Grand Minister Li Pu Ting, a junior official from the Ministry of Personnel, was then suffering from jaundice and should have been treated with a light draining medicine. However, he hesitated due to his lack of heirs. I said: If you have this illness, you should use this medicine. I prescribed Yin Chen Wu Ling Powder with the addition of Qian, Lian, and Shan Zhi, and he recovered. In the year of Xin Mao, he had a son and took my hand, laughing, saying: A doctor's prescription is like a public case; if you avoid slanderous remarks, how could you enjoy your remaining years and entrust them to others? From then on, he treated me with even greater respect.

    The governor of Yingtian suffered from full-body yellowing, spoke wildly, and endured severe chest pain, which was problematic due to blood accumulation in the middle burner. I used a single dose of Tao Ren Cheng Qi Decoction to drain the stagnant blood and he was cured.[113p]
